Jiangxi Education Director Cheng Shih-kuei Announces This Year's Jiangxi Education Policy

(Nanchang Correspondent) As the 23rd year begins, Cheng Shih-kuei, Director of the Jiangxi Education Department, has announced the education policy to inform colleagues in the province's education sector. He mentioned that he has formulated ten educational guidelines to address the national crisis education, provincial crisis education, production education, and character education. He elaborated on the following: (1) The main purpose of national crisis education is to transform the national mindset, stimulate the national spirit, and cultivate national self-confidence. (2) Provincial crisis education aims to train young people's thinking and strengthen the national physique, thereby increasing the people's self-defense capabilities. (3) Production education should promote scientific knowledge, vigorously improve rural areas, and increase local production. (4) Character education should pay attention to the integrity of the academic atmosphere, the rectification of the scholar's habits, and the improvement of folk customs. He concluded by saying that this period is the time for educators to take responsibility. Educators' sole belief lies in consistently believing in the effectiveness of education. What is said above, national crisis education is for saving the country, provincial crisis education is for saving the province, production education is for teaching people, and character education is for saving the nation. These are all the goals and applications of education in the future, and none of them are not the responsibilities of educators. Those who can exert their best efforts will surely find spiritual comfort, and those who have the determination to act vigorously will surely reap practical results. This is also the general principle of service. I, Shih-kuei, would like to inform my colleagues and encourage them to work together and see the results.

Banning Textbooks and Teaching Materials That Cause National Resentment

▲ All Ethnic Groups are Equal, Without Discrimination

▲ The Municipal Education Bureau is Ordered to Notify

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an instruction to schools and magazines in the city, stating: "According to Instruction No. 13967 from the Ministry of Education, the Xinjiang Education Commissioner Huang Wenbi reported that a Mongolian named Bao Yue-gui claimed that some textbooks contained records of Han people killing Mongolians on commemorative days. After investigation, it was found that the elementary school textbooks published around 1926 contained the fact that the Mid-Autumn Festival was a commemorative day for killing Tatars, which caused dissatisfaction among the Mongolian people. Please take measures to ban such or similar records and remarks to avoid causing resentment among ethnic groups." Based on this, the Party advocates that all ethnic groups within the country are equal and without discrimination. Therefore, the Bureau is ordered to strictly ban textbooks containing such records and instruct all schools, bookstores, and magazines to be especially careful when compiling textbooks or citing stories, so as not to include anything that could cause resentment among ethnic groups within the country, in order to uphold the government's consistent intention of harmonizing the feelings of all ethnic groups. This instruction is hereby issued for compliance.

Jinan University School of Business Alumni Association Established Today

The establishment of the School of Business at Jinan University pioneered the establishment of business schools in Shanghai's national universities. It has a long history and has produced many talents. Many of its alumni have been working in various industrial and commercial institutions in Shanghai, but they have rarely been organized and had little contact. The alumni working in various industrial and commercial institutions urgently need to connect in order to seek mutual progress in their careers. Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

The Spirit of Cooperation

— Ren Wei

In my childhood, I remember a passage in my elementary school textbook: "The limbs complained that the mouth only knew how to eat and did not work. The mouth complained that the stomach only knew how to digest food. The stomach complained that the large intestine only absorbed nutrients and did not digest food. As a result, the limbs went on strike, the mouth had no food to eat, the stomach had no food to digest, and the large intestine had no nutrients to absorb. Finally, the limbs could not get the supply of nutrients and could not move." Children! Here is a very appropriate analogy: the limbs are like laborers, the mouth and stomach are like the petty bourgeoisie, and the large intestine is like the big capitalists. There should be no class divisions in society. However, laborers cannot be separated from the petty bourgeoisie; the petty bourgeoisie cannot be separated from the big capitalists; and the big capitalists cannot be separated from the laborers. The relationship between these three is just like the human body, no one can complain about anyone, and no one can be separated from anyone. Unfortunately, each class in society only knows its own selfish interests and lacks the spirit of cooperation. As a result, they will all perish together and run to a path of destruction!

Children! When you grow up, whether you are laborers, petty bourgeoisie, or big capitalists, you must not conflict or fight each other, so that they cannot stand each other. You should take the spirit of cooperation and run together to the bright road!

The Unhygienic Wang Anshi

— Yuan Xifu

Wang Anshi was the Prime Minister of the Song Dynasty. He was very knowledgeable in politics and literature. He once changed the politics of the Song Dynasty, and many of his writings have been passed down. However, he was a person who never paid attention to hygiene.

He does not comb his hair; does not take a bath; and does not change his clothes.

One day, a louse crawled on his beard. His friend said to him, "There is a louse on your beard!" Anshi said in a pedantic manner, "It is occasionally swimming on the Prime Minister's beard, and the Emperor has seen it!"

After speaking, he laughed.

Little Experience

— Jianfen

Calligraphy Practice

Little friends: Are your calligraphy practice books divided into nine squares? When you first started learning calligraphy, did you feel that your copies didn't look like the originals? Now, I'll tell you a very simple method: (1) First, use a piece of glass the same size as the characters on the model; (2) Draw the nine-square grid on the glass with ink; (3) When copying, place the glass with the nine-square grid over the characters on the model; (4) Copy the characters that are projected through the glass onto your nine-square grid practice book, following the grid lines. This way, the copied characters, although not exactly like the originals, will be better than copying without any guidelines.

(Supplementary Note) Little friends: If your practice book is a blank paper book, just use a piece of white paper the same size as the book, draw a nine-square grid on it, and place it under the paper you're using to copy. Then the white paper will also project a nine-square grid.

Steel Pen Nib

When you use a new steel pen (not a fountain pen) or a new steel pen nib, often the nib is dipped in ink, but it doesn't write: (sometimes it might write, but rarely). What is the reason for this? It's probably because the nib is coated with oil from the "pen nib manufacturing machine"...: so it can't write. At this time, you just need to wipe the nib with a piece of paper; it's best to first light a match and burn the nib, then wipe it with paper. This way, the nib will write smoothly.

Little Ant

— Qiu

Little ant, courageous;

Little ant, righteous;

Internally, there is order,

Externally, not bullied;

When fighting, they form groups,

Unite to strive for victory.

Big Snow Flurries

— Qiu

North wind blows, big snow flies,

Snowflakes fill the fields;

Turning into a silver world,

Pure and incomparable;

Wishing for lasting purity,

Do not let it be stained with mud!

Children's Court of Hankou Municipal Primary School

— Zhao Peng

Hankou Municipal First Primary School has very complete facilities. In addition to having a kindergarten, Minsheng Bank, a vending department, and a model village, the school has also established a children's court. The purpose is to cultivate children's legal knowledge and enhance their ability to self-govern. Although the organization is simple, the scale is quite complete, and the work within the court is well-organized. Now, I will introduce the contents of the court below, hoping that the primary school students in this city will try it out.

Female Student Serves as Director

The organization of the court is very simple, consisting of one director, two judges, two clerks, and two bailiffs, all serving in voluntary positions. There are no transportation fees or office expenses, and all positions are held by students.

All Kinds of Naughty Cases

The students of the school are mostly around seven or eight to eleven or twelve years old. Of course, there are inevitably naughty behaviors among the students. Therefore, the cases handled by the court are nothing more than the following: (1) Not returning borrowed books, (2) Not repaying borrowed money, (3) Cursing others, (4) Hitting people for no reason, (5) Snatching food, (6) Writing words with chalk or drawing turtles on others' bodies, (7) Soiling others' clothes, (8) Fighting, (9) Stealing things.

Interrogation Resembles a Court

After the court accepts a case, it schedules a hearing. Both the plaintiff and the defendant must appear in court to present their cases. Sixth-grade students can act as lawyers, representing and defending the parties involved. After the director understands the details of the case, they will judge the severity of the circumstances and issue a verdict, including: recording demerits, compensation, standing as punishment, and apology. If someone makes a false accusation, they will be punished in return.

Training Office as the Supreme Court

If the judgment of a case is unfair or biased, the losing party can appeal to the director of training (i.e., the Supreme Court), and the case will be tried again. After the judgment, it becomes final.

The Wonder of Water

— Xu Zongjie

What we drink and use daily is also something indispensable in life, and that is water. We are so used to it that we don't find it wonderful at all. But upon close examination, we find that nothing in the world is more wonderful than it.

It is a flowing "liquid." Exposed to sunlight, it evaporates and rises, turning into a "gas." When it encounters cold, it freezes into ice, as clear as crystal and as hard as stone, which is a "solid." Is there anything else besides water that can exist in three states: "liquid," "gas," and "solid"?

This is not the only wonderful thing about it. When it evaporates and rises, it turns into raindrops when it encounters cold. When raindrops fall and encounter cold, they turn into six-petaled snowflakes or hailstones the size of soybeans. Water vapor near the ground turns into dew at night; if it gets colder, it turns into frost. In fact, rain, dew, frost, and snow are all magic tricks of water.

Its nature is incomparably calm. It flows downward when tilted. Therefore, scientists use it as a standard for flatness, and call it a "horizontal line."

Water is truly a wonderful thing. Little friends, if you don't believe me, you might as well take a closer look.

Quickly Cut Your Nails

— Ning Ziqiang

Little friends! Do you have nails on your hands? Please cut them clean from today onwards! Why? Nails are a medium for transmitting diseases and a silent killer. How can nails kill? Because when you play with dirty things with your hands, and then grab food and eat voraciously, the disease-causing agents enter your stomach without you even realizing it.

If you eat unclean food, won't you get sick! Cholera! Plague! Diphtheria! Dysentery! If the illness is severe, it can kill, so isn't that a silent killer?

Little friends! Not only should you cut your nails, but you should also wash your hands frequently. Not washing your hands before eating is a way to prevent illness!

Three Arrivals

— Quan Jia

Little friends! Let me tell you a story!

A person went to a friend's house, and they were scheduled to meet at nine o'clock. He was walking hurriedly when he suddenly heard someone shouting, "Nine o'clock has arrived, nine o'clock has arrived." He was very anxious, fearing he would be late, so he asked the person shouting;

"How is it already nine o'clock?"

The person shouting laughed and said, "You're mistaken. I'm shouting "The tavern has arrived." You misheard it as "nine o'clock has arrived.""

Little friends, we must have our eyes, hands, and hearts on the job when we do things. Three arrivals!

Little Mouse Leaves the Hole

— Yan BOGuang

A little mouse said to its mother in the hole: "Mother! I'm going out to play today! Play!"

Its mother said: "When you go outside, never be greedy! Beware of people using delicious things to lure you."

The little mouse quickly replied: "I know!"

As soon as it left the hole, it felt extremely interesting. There were so many fascinating things to see. Suddenly, it saw a beautiful wire cage with a fragrant cake inside. It forgot what its mother had told it and squeezed its body into the cage. Before it had finished eating, it had already locked itself inside. But its mother was still deeply hoping that her son, why doesn't he come back sooner.

Correspondence from Little Rural Friends

— Zi Ming

Withering Wood

Dear little friends:

When the tomb of autumn is completed, the god of winter, baring his fangs and brandishing his iron axe, strikes a menacing pose to start a fire with the world. The lush, vibrant deep forest changes, changes because of him, turning red and yellow. In the end, the branches and leaves fall, leaving only desolation! The wind howls. Fortunately, one or two little birds come to pay their respects, but they are shot by hunters unexpectedly with a "bang," becoming pitiful creatures to be mourned!

I remember an incident three years ago, roughly like this: twenty or thirty soldiers, armed with guns and bayonets, and shouting madly with foreign horns "dida, dida": behind the soldiers were many men, women, old, and young civilians following. I looked closely: everyone surrounded a bare-chested man with his hands tied behind his back: at one point, the bound man knelt down, he just knelt down, and someone jumped out from behind, holding a shiny knife, only vaguely hearing a "stab," the head was a movable watermelon. In that instant, applause and shouts of "kill" sounded like thunder, but the atmosphere of "terror and killing" remained. Those who watched were horrified, as if staying long would lead to the misery of being killed, and they scattered in a puff of smoke: no, there was still a corpse with its hands tied behind its back and no head!

Little friends: Are you sad for this headless man?

You must know that the trees that have shed their branches and leaves are no different under the tyranny of winter.

Withered Grass

Dear little friends:

This world, the world that you and I live in, is constantly changing, moment by moment, moment by moment. Human affairs are like this, and so is nature. Autumn dies and winter is born, the changes in nature are just particularly obvious.

Those trees have been taken to the execution ground; but where have those flowers and grasses gone, which world have they gone to? The fragrant and beautiful flowers once attracted many people's admiration and appreciation: the short grass was like needles, and the green turf was evenly laid out; I remember that not long ago, our truly lively little friends slept, jumped, and danced here. Now the green world is gone. Terrible, this "changing" world!

Several little friends in tattered clothes are carrying a bundle of withered grass. These little friends are probably the children of boatmen from Jiangbei; they may be entrusted by God to specially "collect corpses" for the withered grass everywhere, resulting in "cremation"!

But, there are many flowers and plants that are thriving in the flower room, basking in the sun and heating the water: they sprout, grow, bud, and bloom; but they have never known the taste of "winter". Nor do they know the misery of the other flowers and plants.

Plants also have good fortune and misfortune, strange?

When this letter meets you, it will probably be at the beginning of the year in the Republic of China, so here I wish you

A happy New Year and progress

Children's Corner

New Year

— Han Xiaoxia, a sixth-grade student from Hua Nan Primary School

The New Year is coming, and soon it will bring the bright spring light from the ends of the earth, bestowing it upon us lively and innocent little friends. What a happy thing this is!

But, every time I come home from school, I always see my dear parents sitting face to face with sad faces, or talking and sighing about economic problems of "owing others" and "being owed"... these are also things that make me feel disappointed in addition to happiness.

Last night, my mother sat on the bed and, out of nowhere, told me a story about the New Year. She said: "Nian" is a man-eating beast that appears once every three hundred and sixty days or so. Its purpose is to eat people; so on New Year's Day, people close their doors and stay at home to avoid "Nian". On the second day, everyone goes out to stroll around, and when they meet acquaintances, they greet each other with "Congratulations"... "Closing the door" is to prevent "Nian", and "Congratulations" is to congratulate you for escaping the poisonous mouth of "Nian" and not being eaten by "Nian."

Even now, I still remember it, I remember it very clearly, and I even seem a little scared.

However, when I think of the bright spring light, the new clothes that my mother is sewing for me, and the pastries that my father bought back from the city yesterday, I can't help but dance for joy again.

A Child's Failure

— Ju Chengchang, a thirteen-year-old student from Songjiang

Once upon a time, there was a child playing in the garden, walking back and forth, when suddenly, he saw a sparrow falling on the ground, crying wildly. The child picked up the sparrow with his little hands and looked at it, seeing that one of its legs was broken. The child took some cloth to bandage the broken leg and put it on a tree. After a while, the sparrow flew away.

Later, the sparrow brought a seed and dropped it in the child's garden. After a few days, that seed turned into a watermelon. The child saw this watermelon, and quickly happily picked it, cut it open with a knife, and inside there were big and small pearls and treasures. The child took the pearls to his mother, and his mother was very happy, and the child was also very happy. A child next door heard about it, so he caught a sparrow, broke one of its legs, bandaged it with cloth, and let the sparrow fly away. After a few days, that sparrow also brought a seed and dropped it in his garden. After a few more days, a watermelon also grew. The child was very happy, and he said, "I will also have big pearls..." So he picked it, cut it open with a knife, and a ball of fire came out of the watermelon and burned the child to death.

Securities

Wavering All Day, Bond Prices Rose Little and Fell More

A New Fungkong Trading Company report on the 12th stated that the New York stock market was initially slightly weak, but then rebounded strongly due to good commercial news and strong bond performance. U.S. government bonds surged by one dollar, with strong buying from banks, insurance companies, the government, and private investors. Looking at the overall stock market situation, it may still be inconsistent for the time being. The total daily transaction volume was 1.6 million shares. (Wheat) The public generally believed that the government's monetary policy would be announced next week, leading to substantial purchases and price increases. The situation still favors bullish sentiment. (Cotton) Initially, the opening was firm, but later there were fears that the government would continue to release cotton, and reports on the success or failure of legislation to restrict cotton ginning were contradictory. Bulls tended to liquidate, and the market was depressed. Buyers were still waiting for a rebound. The Foreign Financial Reconstruction Association bought gold at a price of $34.06 per ounce, unchanged. The Dow Jones Index is listed below:

Cotton Yarn

Cotton Yarn Continues to Show Weakness

The yarn market continued to fall, with a rather weak trend. Real demand turned sluggish, and there were unfavorable news regarding current events. As a result, market sentiment was particularly weak. At the same time, British factories offered 4,000 bales of 20-count yarn. Those who accepted it sold it on the market, making the market even looser. However, the cotton market was firm and rising, leaving factories in dire straits.

Man Standard Yarn Continues to Fall by About One Yuan

The Man Standard yarn market opened with a particularly weak market situation. There were fewer buyers. Prices for all months fell by 9 dimes to one yuan. In the afternoon, it was reported that there were few spot yarn transactions, and the market remained weak, falling by 1.2 dimes. The total daily transaction volume was estimated at 14,500 bales. Sales included 1,000 bales of Yu Kang, 1,000 bales of Da Feng, 600 bales of Da Liu, 650 bales of Xie Sheng, and 500 bales of Shen Ji. Purchases included 400 bales of Yuan Tai, 450 bales of Yuan De, 400 bales of De Ji, 650 bales of Tong He, 750 bales of Geng Feng, 450 bales of Ji Feng, and 350 bales of Ren Feng. Yarn Sales Continue to Shrink

Spot yarn sales were less than the previous day. Statistics for all trading groups for the entire day show purchases of only 390 bales. Market conditions weakened. Jardine Matheson offered 4,000 bales of 20-count Five Blessings Shepherd (asking price of 182.5 yuan), sold out for the January and February periods. Guangdong　105　Shantou　45　Southeast Asia　100

Inland　128　Ningbo　　2　Colleagues　　10

The cotton market showed slight signs of softening, with American cotton falling, exchange rates lengthening, and the rising trend of Indian cotton stabilized, with talk of a reaction and decline. Therefore, market sentiment was slightly calmer. Bullish Ningbo traders also realized profits and liquidated 20,000 to 30,000 dan. With this stock being released into the market, the market loosened. However, bullish Shanghai traders tightened their grip and did not release it. The future depends on Indian cotton.

Zheng Standard Cotton Drops Another Two or Three Dimes

The Zheng Standard cotton market opened with bullish Ningbo traders releasing cotton, prices for all months falling by two, three, or four dimes. In the afternoon, market sentiment tightened slightly, with near-month contracts rising by five points and far-month contracts unchanged. The total daily transaction volume was estimated at 100,410 dan. Sales included 4,600 dan of Da Feng, 2,700 dan of Chun Ji, 2,000 dan of Sui Long, 6,700 dan of Chang Feng, 7,300 dan of Yuan Xing Chang, 5,500 dan of Heng De, 1,600 dan of Ren Feng, and 2,900 dan of Yi Cheng. American Cotton Has Fallen Back

Yesterday's American cotton market conditions were inconsistent, with a possibility of a reaction. Initially, prices rose due to spot traders buying, but later fell due to unfavorable news from Liverpool. As a result, spot prices fell by 5 points, and futures prices fell by 10 to 12 points. Liverpool spot cotton was unchanged, and futures fell by 5 or 6 points. Egyptian spot cotton was unchanged. Mumbai cotton cloth fell due to bull liquidation and Japanese sales. As a result, Pinggar rose by 7.5 points, Aumra fell by 7.5 points, and Bairoxi rose by 1 rupee and 2.5 points. The original telegraph record is on the left (12th telegram):

American Cotton Fields Tend to Decrease

A New York telegram on the 12th reported on the cotton market for the week: Last week, the cotton market improved due to increased demand from the industry and speculators. Trading was also active, and the spot position was strong. There is a tendency for a decrease in cotton fields next season, with an upward trend. Bulls have liquidated their positions, and government agents have also occasionally sold cotton to protect their contract privileges. Since the end of last year, prices have risen by about 7.5 points, and bulls have also sold off accordingly. It is reported that farmers are signing up to reduce planting quite quickly. Washington news: The government is planning to increase its power to manage and reduce production. The weekend statistics are attached on the left (unit: 1,000 bales):

Sales of Japanese Factory Yarn Decreased Significantly in December

According to a survey by Japanese trading companies in Shanghai, the total sales of cotton yarn transported from Japanese factories in Shanghai to various places in December 1933 was 27,144 bales, a decrease of 13,128 bales compared to the end of November. Food

The Standard Flour Market Is Quite Dull

After the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for various months showed a trend of initial firmness followed by weakness. With foreign wheat quoted at about two or three dimes higher in Chicago and four or five dimes higher in Canada, the opening price was slightly better than the previous day by half a point. However, trading in each session was exceptionally quiet. Real sales groups had no interest, so market sentiment weakened again. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading in various months was still sluggish. However, factories had different attitudes. With real sales being so sluggish, they naturally could not stubbornly resist. But another part was still holding on. As a result, the current month was unchanged, February was up by 0.5%, March was up by 0.25%, April was unchanged, May was up by 0.5%, and June was up by 1%.

Wheat Futures Are Calm

Yesterday, the wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning and afternoon, generally showed a fluctuating trend for various months. With foreign wheat quoted two, three, four, or five dimes higher, market sentiment was inevitably slightly better. However, with the end of the accounting period approaching, trading companies were doing little trading. Therefore, only the June contract opened at one price in the morning, and the rest were vacant bids. There was slight trading in the afternoon, but there were few movements. As a result, the current month was unchanged, February and April were up by one point, June was unchanged, and the rest were unopened. The spot wheat market, due to scarce arrivals, was gradually bid up. It was reported that over 1,000 bags of Shandong white wheat were opened at a price of 4.05 yuan, purchased by Shen Da.

Measures for Selling American Flour and Wheat

It is heard that the government has had several discussions with people in the flour industry regarding the measures for selling American flour and wheat borrowed by the government, and there are already measures in place. There are approximately 160,000 tons of wheat and 6.4 million bags of flour. Starting next month, they will be shipped to China in batches over a year, so that the effect of adjustment can still be achieved during sales.

Late Rice Sales Stagnant, Slightly Softer by Two Points

(South Shanghai) Sources of supply from various trading groups are still surging, with over 70 vessels arriving continuously (over 10,000 shi). Among them, there are still over 30 ships of late rice, and the guest trading groups' appetite suddenly became stagnant after the market was smoothly handled once yesterday. Unexpectedly, this caused it to turn sluggish. There is currently a state of invisible stagnation. Therefore, market conditions initially seemed to contain a sign of weakness, and sellers were unwilling to easily release them, resulting in a quiet environment. Later, fortunately, those in the trade went to the warehouse to handle it, and about 1,000 bags of green corner, Song, Si, Feng, and Lian goods were sold, and prices slightly improved by two points. The appetite for thick japonica and Du Yang tip rice from various trading groups was slightly more active, and the market also seemed to turn slightly. The overall trend for Chang, Su, Tong, and Nangang goods was able to stabilize slightly, but still contained a soft color. Yin Yuan remains firm due to seasonal influences.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over 20 vessels arrived from various places downriver. Sales of various types on the market are still sluggish and detailed. The market is trending downward daily. White japonica, white yuan, early thin rice, and yin yuan prices are slightly lower by a small margin. Yang Du, Bu Ke, and tip rice are also down by a small number of points.

Guest Indica High-Quality Goods Stable

Yesterday's guest indica market was initially flat and weak, but then there were inquiries from local rice shops. Also, the situation in Fujian Province gradually stabilized, and market sentiment gradually improved. There was an intention to buy and store from various parties. Therefore, the market seemed to be able to gradually turn around. However, there were not many high-quality goods on the market, with medium-quality goods being more abundant. Therefore, high-quality goods were able to hold their ground, while medium-quality goods were still being watched for weakness. Yesterday, a Ningbo trading group purchased 100 bags of Jiangxi machine-milled late rice at a price of 6.55 yuan. Local and account traders purchased 43 bags of Jiangxi machine-milled red rice at a price of 6.54 yuan, 93 bags of Hunan machine-milled red rice at a price of 6.54 yuan, and 560 bags of Jingtian rice at a price of 5.85 yuan to 5.80 yuan. Other transactions were minimal.

Soybean Prices Turn Tight

Yesterday's soybean prices continued to rise by two or three points, actually because sellers' intention to sell turned tight. The source of supply was not surging, the sales channel continued, and market sentiment was firm. Moreover, market prices had fallen to the bottom, causing both buyers and sellers to unanimously view it as good. The atmosphere was very tight. It is hoped that incoming goods will connect but not surge, and sales channels will continue without interruption. The market may see an upward trend in the future. Yesterday, about 11 or 12 carloads of various beans were traded in total. Zhengyangguan beans opened at 3.50 yuan to 4.00 yuan, Xuzhou beans at 3.43 yuan, Huangkou beans at 3.35 yuan, Guidé beans at 3.45 yuan to 3.33 yuan, and Xinyangzhou beans at 3.32 yuan to 3.30 yuan. Dalian beans opened at two carloads, priced at 4.35 yuan, purchased by local traders. 200 bags of Pinghu Du beans opened at prices of 4.90 yuan and 4.77 yuan, which were divided between Ningbo and local traders.

Sugar Market

Chaoqing Falls Sharply, Minor Rebound

Shantou Telegram Reports Another Rise of Three Dimes

Yesterday's sugar market was slow, as it was Saturday and there were no loadings today. The trend was still weak. However, Chaoqing, according to telegrams from Shantou, continued to rise by three dimes, and the quoted prices turned tight. The association quoted a price of 18.95 yuan for No. 24 raw sugar, but there were no takers. Dutch Red Taikoo sugar also quoted the original price, but no transactions were made. The local factory's refined white sugar fell another dime. Zhen Ji No. 1 was 17.9 yuan, No. 2 was 7 dimes, No. 3 was 5 dimes, and No. 4 was 3 dimes. Chaoqing, after the first session of picking up village green came to 15.5 yuan, has fallen by more than 3 yuan step by step. Now, with land prices rising by 5 dimes over the past two days, the quoted prices have shown a slight rebound, opening at about 400 bags, priced at 12 yuan, and 11.9 yuan to 11.6 yuan, up by a corner. There is a continued tightening trend, which can be said to be a sharp fall followed by a minor rebound. New cotton red opened at about a hundred bags, priced at 15 yuan to 14.7 yuan. Diaoqing also brought slightly better news. It was already open yesterday.

Hardware

Association Iron Arrives, Sales Are Strong, but Sluggish

The Association Iron market, recently, due to the slack business of guest trading groups and the lack of procurement by local can factories, cigarette factories, and biscuit companies, the trend is extremely cold. Therefore, the quoted price level is very weak. The price per box, such as old steel factory goods, is estimated at 29.5 yuan, and new steel factory goods open at 28.25 yuan, both looser than before. However, imports are currently very strong, so there are a large number of them stockpiled in various foreign warehouses in Pudong and Puxi. Therefore, the future trend is difficult to be optimistic about.

Purple Copper Yesterday's Telegram Falls by One Yuan

Purple copper received a weak telegram from New York yesterday, so the local market atmosphere was depressed. The standard price fell by one yuan, and the selling price was 44.5 yuan per dan. Only about a hundred dan were traded.

Bamboo Steel Bar Prices Gradually Loosen

Bamboo steel bars were sold yesterday for only 108 yuan, another 2 yuan looser than before. Transactions with construction groups were still good, but procurement by guest trading groups was already scarce. However, arrivals within the year were extremely strong, the market was empty, and the price level was difficult to maintain.

Oil Market

As New Year's Candles Are About to Be Sold, Asphalt Prices Rise

Since the opening of the new asphalt market in Hankou, due to the need for procurement in various places, with thousands of dan being processed in Zhenjiang, Shanghai, Suzhou, and Ningbo, and even procurement in Yichang, the source of supply has turned scarce at this time, resulting in supply not meeting demand. At this time when new goods are in demand, the reason why the source of supply is not strong is not that there are no goods in the production area, but that the rivers in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River are dry, and loading and transportation are not keeping up. Also, candle makers in various places are manufacturing New Year's candles, and the usage is naturally different from usual. They are procuring from Hankou at the same time, and spot goods are therefore insufficient for distribution. The market has also risen accordingly. According to a letter received yesterday from Hankou, Chongjing has been increased to 18 yuan per dan, Pingjing to 17.45 yuan, and Macheng oil to 16.56 yuan, about one yuan higher than the opening price. Local traders have processed 4,000 to 5,000 pieces, which are starting to be shipped continuously. Therefore, the Changjiang ferryboats have had arrivals every day, and sales prices have also been increased based on Hankou prices. Chongjing is selling for 21.78 yuan per dan, Pingjing for about 21 yuan, and Macheng is sold by city weight at 18 yuan plus some change. Zhejiang asphalt has also risen along with it. It is heard that Inner Ping oil is sold for 20.23 yuan, and there is also talk of Lanbai oil being above 16 yuan. It is not known if this is accurate. Zhejiang Western car oil is said to require 21 yuan delivered to Shanghai, which is excessively high. A price of 20.56 yuan by city weight seems fair. Among the local goods, only Jiangxi oil continues to arrive. Yang Chunhe, an old brand, previously opened a guest price of 20.05 yuan, but now it is feared that it will not be less than 21 yuan. As for oils from Wenzhou and Taizhou, the goods are inferior, so the guest price is still within 20 yuan. However, this rise is not entirely driven by candle sales in various places, but also because the Benchang soap factory used about 10,000 dan, resulting in squeezing from both sides.

Free Talk

Auctioning Civilization

— Fengzi

Humanity is truly the most civilized thing. The world has reached a point today where it can't possibly be more enlightened. Even livestock, it is said, should be treated with kindness. Mr. Hitler has banned cruelty to mute animals; the Scottish Secretary of State does not allow disturbance of the Loch Ness monster; and the Japanese Minister of the Army posthumously awarded the highest medal to the military dog that died in the attack on the North Barracks. These three events may be different in circumstances, but they are all grand ceremonies of civilized nations, without a doubt.

When Mr. Hitler first ascended to the throne, his most notable act of virtue was burning books, excluding dissidents, and expelling Jews, followed by this order to protect mute animals. At first glance, it seems a bit comical that these things come from the same person, but in reality, the former are his true intentions, while the latter is just the old trick of "killing and covering up traces."

Civilization must wait for a good price to be sold, but it can also be auctioned off at a discount.

English gentlemen are even more civilized than Mr. Hitler. The Loch Ness monster does not appear often and does not pose a threat to the empire. Moreover, this monster has something that pleases the gentlemen, which is its "strangeness"; therefore, when the announcement was made, "public opinion was greatly relieved," which is also the reason. When Gandhi went to England, English gentlemen flocked to the pier to welcome him; they were not welcoming Gandhi for his ability to fight for freedom for India, but simply to admire this strange Indian skinny elephant. This is exactly the same mentality as welcoming the Haikyo Berman Circus.

So, welcome as they may, India is still India. Kindness has actually reached the livestock, it seems that civilization is only fit to be auctioned off.

The treasure admired by the Japanese Minister of the Army is the military dog. Since it is a meritorious dog, it should be treated equally. Moreover, Japan is a rising civilized nation. However, calling a dog a military dog is too blatant. Moreover, the blood of the North Barracks, the corpses of Shenyang, and even the skeletons of the four provinces are said to be compatriots of ours. But the price of civilization is too extravagant for these compatriots, and this benefit is instead taken by livestock.

Chinese people probably still have to appreciate these civilizations with tears in their eyes.

However, as long as they are high-class or upper-class Chinese, they actually still have an "inherent" civilization, which is "gentlemen eat meat but stay away from the kitchen." But this is not auctioned off.

To put it more bluntly, it's not even worth talking about auctioning.

On Realistic Novels in Response to Mu Mutian

— Chen Junye

The issue of "Realistic Novels and First-Person Writing" has already sparked serious discussion, which, as Mr. Mu said, is not without its benefits. Therefore, even though Mr. Mu and I still hold different opinions, I still have something to say. I must first clarify that Mr. Mu and I do not have different arguments. If the arguments were different, the discussion would be less meaningful.

(1) In "Further Discussion on Realistic Novels and First-Person Writing," Mr. Mu believes that "in the current culturally backward China, writing novels about peasants and workers in the first person is more likely to become glib." I believe that Mr. Mu's understanding includes many incorrect tendencies. This can easily develop into the idea that novels depicting peasants and workers should only appear after Chinese culture has improved and peasants and workers themselves can write novels. Needless to say, this is a wrong understanding and a very dangerous one. If we want to trace the root of this error, it is nothing more than standing on the viewpoint of analytical realism (there is no doubt that Mr. Mu has been deeply influenced by Flaubert's thinking), believing that only reflecting objective reality in a photographic manner is beneficial to truth, and that "Yang Ma's Diary" must be written by Yang Ma herself, and must be written so clumsily to be considered true. However, only those simple bystanders are satisfied with this vulgar naturalism or analytical realism. Mr. Mu is precisely one of these bystanders (his theory proves it). He boldly separates peasants and workers from the author, placing them in two different positions. The author is never completely irrelevant to the characters in the work, but only observes and expresses them with a bystander's attitude. I cannot but say that this understanding is the greatest crisis in Mr. Mu's thinking.

(2) In the past, the first-person writing style was commonly used by romantic writers as a means of expressing their individualism and lyricism. I have long admitted this fact. However, when the first-person writing style is used in new content (expressing the emotions of the peasant and worker class), it can no longer be regarded as a form of individualistic lyricism. Due to its different essence, its form has been transformed in a new direction, and it can no longer be called an old form. Mr. Mu cited Bedny's use of the fable poetry form to write many popular poems, and even admitted that its content was new, but its fable poetry form was still old. This is an even more incorrect understanding. If we examine the differences between Bedny's fable poems and other ancient fables, we can obtain proof. When an old form is suitable for new content and is adopted as a means of expression, this form is no longer old. I dare to repeat a sentence here. If we do not grasp the whole and its dynamic characteristics in our understanding of a problem, we will inevitably fall into the narrow path of bourgeois one-sided understanding and knowledge.

(3) Regarding the issue of the truthfulness of literature, Mr. Mu said that it is inversely proportional to the amount of complex reality reflected in it. From this sentence, I believe that Mr. Mu is again committing the fundamental defect of naturalist theory. The acquisition of the truthfulness of literature lies in grasping the practical knowledge of sensual human activity. Naturalists determine it by describing the quantity of the scope, so the characteristic of naturalist literature is to observe and list all things regardless of value. Their purpose is to be all-encompassing, and they believe that they can obtain objective "truth" in that way, which has resulted in the precision and tediousness of naturalism to an infinite extent. Is this also the amount that Mr. Mu requires for literary truthfulness? If we measure the truthfulness of a literary work, and we only observe the scope it describes to determine its level, wouldn't it be a joke? Regarding this issue, Mr. Mu's criticism of me has not only failed to obtain a more advanced theory, but has instead increased incorrect views, which makes me sincerely regret it.

(4) Regarding the issue of first-person writing and realistic novels, we must stand on socialist realism in order to grasp the correct understanding. Merely staying in naturalist realism, strolling in the area of pure bystanderism, and only knowing to explore techniques and forms for realism, I can judge that he will never obtain a bright path to walk on. The realism of Balzac, Zola, etc. is not what we require now. What we now require is comprehensive realism!

New Year's Eve

— Chen Fuxi

New Year's Eve.

In a warm room, a young couple is having a sumptuous dinner. The room is quiet, with only the two of them—

"Jane, I'll pick a piece of chicken for you, the chicken is especially delicious today..."

The wife didn't respond, nor did she nod.

Filled with melancholy, this silent room:

She sits, frowning, remembering something she had forgotten. She doesn't , nor does she drink alcohol; painful memories keep disturbing her mind. Her face is pale, thin, and haggard, suffering from severe hysteria. She is already in her thirties, but she looks like she is in her forties; but she still has no children...

Tonight, she sits at the table, unable to eat anything. Although the table is full of fish, meat, and chicken, which are fresh, oily, and delicious, her throat always feels like it is blocked with a cork.

She can't even swallow a drop of soup.

The husband didn't hear his wife's answer, so he said again:

"Why are you so unhappy?"

"No, I'm very happy..."

She reluctantly raised her head and shook it a few times; then, she lowered her head again. For a long time: Crystal tears dripped down from her eyes in strings.

The room is quiet.

He watched his wife cry, no longer in the mood to drink. His heart was also in turmoil. He really didn't understand her, why was she sobbing at this New Year's Eve dinner? He also didn't know what she was so sad about? He just stared at her, dumbfounded, with many words he wanted to say, but even one sentence was difficult to utter. He didn't know how to say it to comfort her, to stop her sobbing?

"Jane, why are you crying? Tonight is New Year's Eve, we should be happier..."

"Yes, we should... I don't want to anymore..."

"Think about what?" the husband immediately asked.

"Think about our little baby..."

The wife couldn't continue, her voice trembling. Hearing these words, all the sorrow in the husband's stomach welled up in his heart, making him unable to suppress it. However, seeing his wife cry, seeing his wife stunned, he had no choice but to say to her:

"Don't think about her anymore, tonight is New Year's Eve..."

As he spoke, he involuntarily picked up his wine glass and drank several sips in a row.

The wife cries...

The room is quiet.

Because he drank too much wine, the husband was almost drunk. The husband's eyes were red, and he was almost crying too.

After drinking a lot of wine, he suddenly remembered something and asked:

"If our little baby didn't die, how old would she be?"

"Ah ha! Have you forgotten?" the wife said, crying, her voice still trembling.

"Forgot! Completely forgot!"

"Eh, have you really forgotten? Our little baby's zodiac sign is Rabbit!... "

"Hmm, that's right! If she didn't die, she would already be..."

He only said half of the sentence before he poured the wine glass to his lips again.

The room is quiet.

Wells's Prophecy: A Record of the Sino-Japanese War in 1935

— Meng Zhen

With the arrival of the New Year, prophecies have become very popular for a time, and several magazines are requesting prophecies for 1934. Originally, we live in such an enlightened world, what else can we say? So, we can only predict the future.

HG Wells's prophecy was reported by Reuters in September, and I remember that the newspapers in Shanghai all published it. In addition to being a historian, the author of "The Outline of History" is also known as a socialist, civilization critic, and popular novelist. There is no need for any introduction, and I think everyone knows it. But what is particularly worthy of our attention is his scientific observation, far-reaching imagination, and sharp criticism. Therefore, since the publication of his prophetic novel "The Shape of Things to Come," it immediately aroused excitement among readers around the world.

Recently, this book has also arrived in China. According to his own description, this is like his previous book, "A Short History of the World" (translated by Fan Zhongyun, published by Commercial Press), which is a future short history describing the 150 years from 1913 to 2116. He pretends that it is Dr. Raveu's dream book, as if it is just a "castle in the air prophecy," but in fact, it has a very strong realistic color, especially the first volume, "Today and Tomorrow," which is simply a history of the past twenty years. The second volume and below are about the future, but the writing and arguments are based on scientific and economic theories, so even if it is a dream, it can be said to be a scientific dream.

The entire book is divided into five volumes, first describing the arrival of the collapse period (Volume 1), followed by the collapse period, the third is the revival of the world, that is, the birth of modern countries, the fourth is the modern national movement, and the fifth is the life jointly managed by modern countries, about 200,000 words. According to his prophecy, the world war in the 1940s was within the collapse period, and the prelude to it was the Sino-Japanese War in 1935, which later turned into the US-Japanese War. By 1939, it ended with Japan's defeat. After the world war, the capitalist world that only sought self-interest collapsed completely, and by the 21st century, it embarked on the road of building a new world. (To be continued)

Two Brothers (8) (5)

— Written by Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

When she brought the wine, he said again:

"I came specifically to say goodbye to you. I'm going out."

She replied without paying attention:

"Ah, ah! Where are you going?"

"America."

"I heard it's a beautiful country."

She didn't say anything else. Really, it was really rash to talk to her today. There were really too many people in the coffee shop today.

So Pierre went out and walked towards the beach. When he walked to the embankment, he saw the "Pearl" fishing boat carrying his father and Captain Boziru back. The sailor Babagri was rowing the oars; the two people sat at the stern with a very happy look on their faces, smoking their pipes. The doctor looked at them passing by, thinking in his heart: "Simple-minded people are really happy."

So he sat on a stool on the breakwater, trying to numb himself into a beastly semi-sleep state.

When he returned home in the evening, his mother didn't dare to raise her eyes to look at him, she just said to him:

"You need to buy a lot of things before you leave, but I don't know where to start. I just ordered some shirts and trousers for you, and told the tailor to come and make clothes for you; but don't you need anything else, don't you need something I haven't thought of?"

He opened his mouth to say: "No, I don't need anything." But he thought he had to at least accept the clothes that would make him look decent, so he replied in a very quiet voice:

"I don't know yet; I'll have to ask at the company."

He went to ask, and someone gave him a list of necessities. When his mother took the list from his hand, it was the first time in a long time that she looked at him, and there was a kind of pleading expression in her eyes, so humble, so gentle, so sad, like a poor dog begging for mercy after being beaten.

On October 1st, the "Lorraine" mail ship sailed from Saint-Nazaire into the port of Havre, so that it would sail from there to New York on the 7th of the same month: and Pierre Roland had to live in that small floating room, where his life would be imprisoned afterwards.

The next day, when he went out, he met his mother on the stairs, and she said to him softly in a voice that was almost inaudible:

"Don't you want me to help you arrange your room on the ship?"

"No, thank you, it's all arranged."

She muttered:

"I really want to see your room."

"No need to see it. It's very ugly and very small."

He passed by, leaving her there devastated and leaning against the wall, pale.

But it was old man Roland who had visited the "Lorraine" mail ship that day, and he talked about this magnificent ship at dinner, and he was quite surprised that his woman had no intention of taking a look, because their son was going to take this mail ship.

In the following days, Pierre simply wasn't often home. He was neurasthenic, easily angered, cold-blooded, and his rude words seemed to whip everyone. But on the day before he left, he suddenly appeared very different, appearing very gentle. When he embraced and kissed his parents before going to sleep on the ship for the first time, he asked them:

Amateur Coffee House

Is it Business Acumen?

— Han Dehui

If you want to save trouble and go to a clothing store to buy a newly made or original dress, the shop assistant will definitely take out many new and old clothes of different materials and colors for you to choose from, and very politely ask you to try them on. When you put the clothes on your body, he will definitely make an unexpected expression of joy, saying: "Sir! This dress seems to be specially made for you, it couldn't be more perfect, it couldn't fit better!" If you think it's too short, he will say: "Sir! Look down at yourself!" When you lower your head and bend forward, the front of the dress will also droop down, and naturally you won't feel it's short. If you think it's too long, he will say: "Sir! Your body is not straight enough!" When you straighten your body according to his words, the front of the dress will naturally be raised, and you won't feel it's long; but the back droops down and sweeps the ground, but you don't have eyes in the back, so you can't see it. After his directing, you are indeed satisfied, and then the transaction is successfully completed. As for whether this dress fits well or not, that's another matter; in short, he has made this business.

Ladies and gentlemen go to silk and satin shops to buy clothing materials, and they always want to get a little discount on the size. For example, if she wants to buy ten feet of clothing material, when the shop assistant measures ten feet and is about to cut it off, she hurriedly grabs it with her hand and doesn't allow the scissors to cut, saying: "Let go! Let go! Let go! Let go!" Two inches is not enough, four inches is not enough, six inches is still not enough, eight inches is still not enough, and even letting go by more than a foot is satisfying. If you don't agree, she will not only scold you for being too inflexible in business, but she may also pout, puff out her cheeks, and walk away angrily carrying her money bag. Therefore, in order to make the transaction, the shop assistants let go when they are told to, and they don't dare to cut until she is not very insistent on letting go. But when she returns home and measures the clothing material herself with a ruler, isn't it still ten feet? How much more did she gain from arguing? Originally, the shop assistants knew the temper of the ladies and gentlemen well, and they deducted one inch from each foot when measuring,

The foot that was let go later had already been reserved in advance; because if they didn't do so, this business would be taken away by another store.

I don't know if the above two things are what is called "business acumen"?

Life

Eating Chicken Tails

— Chen Geng

I was opening the new ledger that I had just received in the workshop when the boy Ah Bao jumped in and said, "Mr. Chen, that doctor who vaccinates against smallpox is here again."

"Hmm, where is he?"

"In the manager's office."

In the manager's office, a table was laid out with large and small bottles, as well as sharp, shiny probes. One was wearing a Chinese cotton robe, one was wearing Western clothes, and another was a woman wearing a white coat. They said they were all doctors.

"Thank you for your hard work," the manager said to the one wearing Western clothes.

"It's okay, I'm just doing this job. It's unlucky to be assigned to the factory area, dealing with scary workers..." He replied.

The woman shrugged her shoulders and looked at the clock on the wall: "Mr. Manager, will you get vaccinated? If you want to, I'll do it for you first. The furniture is cleaner at this time."

"Hehehehehe, okay, thank you, but, hehe, there's also my wife. She hasn't been vaccinated since she was a child, hehe, I'd also like to trouble you." The manager said with a smile, unbuttoning his collar as he ordered someone to invite the manager's wife from the back.

First, the doctor wearing the cotton robe applied a layer of lotion to the manager's thick, fat arm, then the female doctor vaccinated him, and then the doctor wearing Western clothes covered him with a bandage. Then, the manager's wife, the deputy manager... were all vaccinated, the same thick, fat arms, the same perfect surgery.

It's the staff's turn to get vaccinated. They came in and out of the manager's office very quickly. Did they use a different, simpler surgery to vaccinate the junior staff? But it's the same vaccination, isn't it? Hmm, no money?

But some people were unwilling to get vaccinated, pretending to go to the toilet to urinate.

Unfortunately, I was called by the deputy manager to get vaccinated. I was very unwilling in my heart, but I didn't dare to disobey the good intentions of my superiors. I took off my long gown in the workshop, passed through the corridor, passed through the square, and it was terribly cold. A minute later, I enjoyed the right to get a free vaccination. However, at the moment of vaccination, the doctor's nose seemed to sense something strange. I can only blame myself for not taking a bath for two weeks, and my undershirt and jacket were all dirty. However, it is also true that I don't have time to take a bath. Who doesn't like cleanliness? Who doesn't pay attention to hygiene? But, you also need time to pay attention to cleanliness and hygiene.

So I ran out of the manager's office in embarrassment.

"Mr. Chen, are you happy? The female doctor vaccinated you, haha!" The driver of car number sixteen joked with me with a hippie smile. Joked, who knows the anger in my stomach.

After the staff was finished, it was the workers' turn.

The boy Ah Bao jumped in first, but was immediately scolded out by the manager because he didn't remove the bird-hunting hat on his head, which was too impolite.

"Does it hurt?"

"It's just like a mosquito bite."

"They say they're doctors, but they're so rough."

"They're naturally not polite to us workers."

………………………

After the male workers were finished, it was the female workers' turn.

But none of the female workers went. Think about it, how could the girls not be shy about taking off their clothes in the manager's office? As a result, only a few young girls were called in.

The doctors left, and six out of ten in the whole factory were vaccinated. You look at my arm, and I look at your arm. What did you see? Aren't they just the same two fresh blood marks, with no cover and no gauze bandage, exposed, blown by the cold wind, and stained by dust. Old Wang said: "After getting vaccinated, you have to eat fresh food, eat chicken, the more the better." The cook Ah Wu said: "A pair of chickens were killed, weighing two catties and four taels, but, hehe! They were killed for the manager's wife to eat."

Manuscript Fees and Life

— Shi Ying

In the afternoon of January 8, 1934, at 3:20 PM.

In front of the window of the accounting department on the second floor of the Shen Bao newspaper office, a crowd of people who lived off manuscript fees were packed together - old, young, male, and female.

The accounting department window was a small hole, just like a ticket window at a train station, with the words "…count clearly in person, no claims accepted after leaving…" written on it. Inside the window sat the clerks wearing glasses, two, three, four of them, the sounds of foreign money and abacuses constantly flying from the window to the outside.

×　　×　　×　　×　　×

I walked over, and there were already many people, at least twelve or thirteen. Quickly, the dialogue of two voices flew past my ears.

"Old Li, when did you arrive?"

"I've been here for a long time. I came yesterday and didn't get paid."

"How many articles do you have?"

"Three."

"Probably more than ten yuan."

"I don't know. They say the first article pays more. I only had one published at the top. Last time I had four and received eight yuan and forty cents."

×　　×　　×　　×　　×

Someone left the window, looking like a worker. The person called Old Li immediately squeezed forward. Then two more people walked up from downstairs. Several people in student attire nodded, smiled, and started chatting while shaking hands. The two newcomers became the center of the conversation. They talked about manuscript fees, literature, the *Eastern Miscellany*, and middle school students. As the conversation became more and more lively, they also talked about Lu Xun, Mao Dun, Zhou Shoujuan, and Zhang Henshui. This was a very brief literary salon.

The person called Old Li passed the seal he used when submitting his manuscripts through the window, his eyes following the accountant's hands as they moved. His eyes moved from the ledger to the abacus, and then to the banknotes. Finally, he received the money, totaling five yuan and twenty cents. He hesitated for a moment, seemingly wanting to get more.

×　　×　　×　　×　　×

"Old Li! You can see two more movies!" A burst of laughter.

"Movies! This is for eating!"

Old Li left, and then I took his place. There were more than a dozen other candidates behind me. As soon as I walked out, these words appeared in my mind: "Ah! This is for eating!"

Commentary

Regarding the Question of "What is Our Guiding National Ideology?"

— Zhiping

In the 57th issue of this journal, Mr. Gongpu posed an important question to us: "What is our guiding national ideology?" Although I do not have "the talent to govern a country," I can be considered a member of the citizenry, and I should contribute my opinion based on the principle that "the rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every citizen."

In China, where everything is chaotic and nothing is unified, if we bring up the question of "what is our guiding national ideology" for discussion, we can get many different answers: the guiding national ideology of the Three Principles of the People, the guiding national ideology of social democracy, the guiding national ideology of Fascism, the guiding national ideology of Bolshevism, the guiding national ideology of nationalism… All of these are specific answers to this question. But the problem is here: among this large batch of answers, which one is correct? That is, which one can build China, revitalize China, and be worthy of being called a guiding national ideology?

Dr. Hu Shih once told us, "Study more problems and talk less about isms." Although I cannot agree with this "divide and conquer" method, in these times, I dare not believe in any ism, let alone discuss anything under it. Therefore, my answer to the question of "what is our guiding national ideology" cannot and dares not say what ism is worthy of being our guiding national ideology. I can only first follow Dr. Hu's method, and first propose several fundamental problems in China to study, and then make an overall solution to the problems.

First, everyone knows that China is a semi-colonial country, and all of China's economic and political rights are controlled by imperialists. China's poverty and all of China's disasters are caused directly and indirectly by the imperialists. Therefore, China should not talk about nation-building, but if it wants to talk about nation-building, it must fight desperately with imperialism, completely abolish all unequal treaties, implement true tariff autonomy, and even fundamentally overthrow the imperialist rule over China, in order to strive for the complete independence of the Chinese nation!

Second, the unresolved land problem in China is the main reason for the bankruptcy of the rural economy, social unrest, and the withering of industry. Therefore, to enable China to maintain the normalcy of a country and develop side by side with the advanced countries of the world, it is necessary to completely solve the land problem, stabilize the countryside, and increase rural purchasing power, in order to prosper the entire national economy.

Third, most of China's citizens are currently under the threat of unemployment, poverty, hunger, and so on. If China is to be worthy of being called a truly civilized country, it must first completely solve all problems of production and distribution and fundamentally eliminate those phenomena.

Fourth, under the solution of the above three problems, we can talk about developing Chinese industry, thereby popularizing education, developing culture, so that China is worthy of being called a modern civilized country, and washing away the shame of "all backwardness."

The above four points are the several fundamental problems of Chinese society that are currently blocking the majority of our compatriots and demanding a solution. Any ism that can solve these fundamental problems can be used as our guiding national ideology. Conversely, an ism that cannot solve these fundamental problems, or even hinders the solution of these problems, is a national destruction ideology.

Of course, no matter what thought or ism, it must be the product of society or a group of people, and it must be implemented by people. Around all isms are many people. The so-called ism that can solve the current fundamental problems in China, that is, the ism that is worthy of being called our guiding national ideology, must also be implemented by many people. In the current China, who can implement this? That is, who are the ones who truly have that kind of guiding national ideology, and who can truly solve the current fundamental problems in China? I don't know. However, I think, if everyone is not forgetful, they should remember that since "September 18th," among the general citizens of China, who are the most capable of resisting Japan and opposing imperialism, and who are the most capable of fighting for the solution of the current fundamental problems in China.

As for which books and publications can represent our guiding national ideology in the current China, it is also difficult to say. It is best to ask everyone to observe according to the above principles—as long as it is supported by the masses who can solve all the current fundamental problems in China, and represents their consciousness, it is a publication or book that represents our guiding national ideology.

Amateur Arts

Nationalist Art and Theater Troupes

— A Member

Many people regard art as a pleasure for a few, but history tells us that art is also produced by human beings for practical needs. Primitive people created writing and sculpture to help their memory, and music and poetry can be said to have originated in this way to forget the fatigue of labor and to match the rhythm of work, from the initial "Hang Yu" sounds to the present.

Each nation has its own special component of art. And this unique art is the nourishment for each nation's own spirit. At the same time, national art must also be the soul of the nation. This is not because of other reasons; all races, bloodlines, modes of production, and geographical environments are the reasons for the formation of special art.

Therefore, in this era of survival of the fittest among nations, we must grasp our own national art, promote it, and make it become the greatest driving force of the nation.

Drama, in China, has a very long history: Yuan opera, Kun opera, Peking opera, Han opera, all the way to Shanghai's "civilized drama"... But most of these things are "the remnants of feudalism." We naturally cannot take them as good nourishment for the nation, let alone promote national progress. Therefore, the emergence of the spoken drama movement is really a good phenomenon of emerging culture.

Drama is generally considered a comprehensive art in art theory, so it is the most suitable mass art. However, the public performances of emerging dramas in the past have not only been very weak, but have also only been the playthings of a part of the intellectual class. I hope that every theater troupe will become a mass art organization and use reality to promote our increasingly declining old nation.

Postal Agency in Another Location

The Final Order

— Fu Fusheng

Guilin, Guangxi Correspondence

Because I am an intellectual, I was promoted to sergeant squad leader in less than two months after joining the army; but as a squad leader, the responsibility is of course heavier. For example, one small thing, the problem of distributing side dishes for each meal, a squad of more than a dozen people, the kitchen only has a large bowl of dishes, and I, as the squad leader, have to distribute them to each person. If I occasionally distribute them unevenly, they will complain, and even many misunderstandings will arise. About four or five months ago, when our troops were marching in the border area of ×× province, the common people ran away at the news, and took all the things they ate and used with them. As a result, we couldn't buy rice for several days in a row, so we had to find some melon vegetables and taro to cook and fill our stomachs. I remember that at that time, our battalion commander's horse died of illness and was abandoned on the side of the road. People from each company almost started shooting at each other in order to fight for the meat of this dead horse. This shows how serious the problem of eating is. Talking about the problem of sleeping is even more unspeakable. There are often times when we sleep on the lawn or under the eaves of the street, and in the middle of the night, there is a torrential rain, soaking our bodies, it is really unbearable. As for our officers, the situation is different. All units above the company level have small kitchens. If they arrive in a place where they can't buy food, they have canned food. If they pass through prosperous towns, they always eat chicken, fish, and other delicacies. The general soldiers have not received their salary for several months, and the one or two yuan of pocket money they receive each month is still saved from the food expenses. Where do they have the money to enjoy the pleasures of the palate?

The above is a glimpse of the suffering of soldiers' lives. The following will talk about the situation during combat.

Since I started living in the army, I have participated in several formal battles. Once, our regiment was assigned as the vanguard, and our company was rotated to serve as the point man. One morning, while searching and advancing, we were discovered by the enemy's sentry. The enemy bugler blew his horn to inquire about us, so we scattered and lay down, and started shooting. In less than half an hour, the two sides' firing lines spread for more than a mile, and the sound of artillery and gunfire shook the heavens and the earth. As a result of this battle, more than 300 of our brothers were killed or injured. Some had their heads blown open, some had their intestines ruptured, and some were lying on the ground, writhing and groaning, asking for a shot to be put out of their misery. Another time, we fought bitterly for a day and a night, and the battle line did not advance. Although the division commander repeatedly issued orders to "save ammunition and advance quickly," still few people were effective. Suddenly, the division commander came to a hilltop and sternly instructed our regimental commander: "At 8:00 tonight, a general attack on the entire line. Everyone must
